Need Between Parts and Avoiding Circularity
The author explains the necessity of need between parts and the condition to avoid circularity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the condition that must be met for the mutual need between parts of a composite to avoid circularity.

Core Idea
Two-sided need from different aspects avoids circularity.

In this passage, the author establishes a foundational principle for analyzing composite entities: the parts necessarily need each other, but this need must not lead to circular reasoning. He distinguishes between one-sided need (which would be circular) and two-sided need from different aspects (which is permissible). The classic example of matter and form illustrates how two different aspects of need can exist without circularity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the concise style and the logical structure.
The passage uses parentheses for commentary insertions.
2
Identify the key condition
Look for the condition that prevents circularity: the need between parts must be either one-sided or two-sided from different aspects. Why is one-sided circular?
The author explicitly says need from two directions is permissible because there is no circularity.
3
Study the example of matter and form
Examine the example: matter needs form for its persistence, and form needs matter for its individuation. These are two distinct aspects, so no circularity.
This is a concrete illustration from physics.
4
Reflect on the broader principle
Consider how this principle applies to other composite entities. Why must need be from different aspects?
This prevents logical circularity in causal explanations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثاني - المقصد العاشر : وجوب حاجة بعض الأجزاء إلى بعض قطعاً، وذلك مما لا يقول به عاقل . ( ثم إنه يجب أن تكون الحاجة ) بين الأجزاء إما من جانب واحد، أو من الجانبين ( بحيث لا يستلزم الدور)، وذلك، أعني استلزامها الدور، ( بأن يحتاج كل جزء إلى الآخر من جهة واحدة، وأما) احتياج كل جزء إلى الآخر ( من جهتين فجائز)، إذ لا دور فيه ( كما تحتاج الهيولى ) إلى الصورة (من وجه، وهو أن بقاء الهيولى بالصورة (و) تحتاج (الصورة) إلى الهيولى ( من ) وجه (آخر)، وهو احتياجها في تشخصها إلى الهيولى ( وسيأتي ) ذلك في موقف الجواهر.
The second observatory - the tenth objective: The necessity of some parts needing others, absolutely, and that is something no rational person would say. (Then it is necessary that the need) between the parts is either from one side, or from both sides (such that it does not entail circularity), and that, I mean its entailing circularity, (is that each part needs the other from one direction, and as for) the need of each part for the other (from two directions, it is permissible), since there is no circularity in it, (just as matter) needs form (from one aspect, which is that the persistence of matter is through form, and) form needs matter (from another aspect), which is its need for individuation from matter, (and that will come) in the station of substances.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage defines the necessity of need between parts of a composite and the condition to avoid circularity. It begins by stating that the need is absolute and no rational person denies it. Then it explains that the need must be either one-sided or two-sided in a way that does not lead to circularity. Circularity would occur if each part needed the other from one direction; but if each needs the other from two different directions, it is permissible because there is no circularity. The example given is matter and form: matter needs form for its persistence, and form needs matter for its individuation. This is two-sided need from different aspects, so no circularity. The passage ends by noting that this will be discussed further in the station of substances.

Key Terms
حاجة
أجزاء
دور
هيولى
صورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any two-sided need necessarily implies circularity.
Correction: Two-sided need is circular only if the need is from the same aspect. If from different aspects, it is permissible, as shown by matter and form.

Checkpoint
What condition must the need between parts satisfy to avoid circularity?
A) It must be one-sided.
B) It must be two-sided from the same aspect.
C) It must be two-sided from different aspects.
D) It must be absolute.

Key Takeaway
Need between parts is necessary, and it avoids circularity only when each part needs the other from a different aspect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a relationship in your life where you and another person need each other. Are those needs from the same aspect or different aspects? Does this lead to unhealthy circularity (e.g., codependence)? What steps can you take today to ensure your dependencies are from different aspects, as the passage teaches, so that the relationship remains healthy and avoids circularity?
?
Reflect on your need for Allah. Unlike the two-sided need in the passage, your need for Him is absolute from every aspect, while He needs nothing from you. How does this asymmetry affect your sense of reliance and gratitude? In what specific ways can you live today as if you truly believe that your entire existence and every good thing comes from Him alone?

The Philosophers' Proof: Specific Difference as Cause of Genus
Philosophers' proof that specific difference is cause of genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that in a composite essence, the specific difference must be the cause of the genus.

Core Idea
In a real composite essence, one part must cause another; genus cannot cause species, so specific difference causes genus.

The philosophers begin by establishing that a composite essence like one comprising genus and specific difference has real unity. This unity implies a causal relationship between its parts. They then argue that the genus cannot be the cause, as that would lead to absurd consequences, forcing the conclusion that the specific difference is the cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key premise
Read the opening statement: a composite essence has real unity, so its parts must have a need relation.
2
Understand the causal implication
From the need relation, one part must be the cause of the other. Recognize that cause here means that on which the other depends.
3
Examine why genus cannot be cause
The author lists two absurdities if genus were cause: the genus would be confined to one species, and opposite specific differences would be necessary for one thing. Both are false, so genus cannot be cause.
4
Conclude the specific difference as cause
Thus, the only remaining possibility is that the specific difference is the cause of the genus, which is the desired conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ المقصد العاشر : وجوب حاجة بعض الأجزاء إلى بعض ] ( قال الحكماء : قد ظهر وجوب حاجة بعض الأجزاء إلى بعض) في الماهية الواحدة وحدة حقيقية ولا شك أن الماهية المركبة من الجنس والفصل حقيقة واحدة كذلك، فلا بد أن يكون بينهما حاجة ) فأحدهما علة للآخر، وليس الجنس علة للفصل وإلا (استلزمه وكان الجنس منحصراً في نوع واحد أو نقول : كانت الفصول

قوله : ( ولا شك إلخ) أشار بتقدير هذه المقدمة إلى أن في عبارة المتن إيجاز الحذف بالقرينة الحالية، وهذا على رأي القائلين بأن الأجزاء المحمولة متغايرة في الخارج ماهية، سواء كانت متحدة وجوداً أو لا، وأما على رأي القائلين بالانتزاع فليس في الخارج إلا الهوية البسيط، والتركيب منهما في الذهن اعتباري .
قوله : ( حقيقة واحدة كذلك ) أي بالوحدة الحقيقية أي مع قطع النظر عن اعتبار المعتبر، أما على رأي القائلين بتركب الماهية من الأجزاء المحمولة في الخارج، فاتصافها بالوحدة في الخارج، وأما على رأي القائلين بأنها انتزاعية والتركب إنما هو في الذهن، فاتصافها بها في الذهن.
قوله : ( وكان الجنس منحصراً إلخ لأنه علة بحسب مقارنتها بالمعلول لتركيب الماهية الحقيقية منهما، فلا توجد طبيعته مفارقة عنه، فإن نظر إلى أن الطبيعة الواحدة لا تقتضي أمرين
قوله: (إما من جانب واحد يمكن إدخاله في عدم استلزام الدور، لكن الأظهر أن قوله : بحيث لا تستلزم الدور فيما يكون الاحتياج من الجانبين. قوله : ( ولا شك أن الماهية المركبة من الجنس والفصل حقيقة واحدة كذلك قيل : إن جعل حقيقة خبراً لأن يكون القضية مهملة؛ لأن من المركبات ماهي اعتيادية، وهي غير ملائمة، فالوجه أن يجعل تمييزاً أو حالاً، وواحدة هي الخبر حتى تكون القضية كلية لا مهملة.
قوله : ( فأحدهما علة للآخر المراد من العلة ما يتوقف عليه الشيء في الجملة، فيتناول الشرط، ولا يرد الاعتراض به نعم يندفع قوله : وليس الجنس علة للفصل الخ، كما سیصرح به . قوله : ( أو نقول الخ المراد من الترديد التخبير بين العبارتين في إلزام الفساد.

المتقابلة لازمة لشيء واحد، وكلاهما باطل . ( فالفصل علة للجنس ) وهو المطلوب . ( وأجيب عنه بأن المحتاج إِليه ) هو ( العلة الناقصة وأنها غير مستلزمة ) لمعلولها، ) فإن أردت بالعلة ( العلة ( التامة منعنا كون أحدهما علة للآخر، ( والحاجة) التي يجب ثبوتها بين الأجزاء ( لا تستلزمه ) أي كون أحدهما علة تامة للآخر، وهو ظاهر. ( وإن أردت ( بالعلة العلة ( الناقصة ؛ فلعل الجنس علة ) ناقصة للفصل، ولا يجب استلزامها المعلولها ، ( إنما المستلزم) للمعلول ( هي العلة التامة)، فلا يلزم انحصار الجنس في نوع واحد ولا كون الفصول المتقابلة لازمة لشيء واحد.
The tenth objective: The necessity of some parts needing others. The philosophers said: The necessity of some parts needing others has become manifest in a single essence with real unity, and there is no doubt that the essence composed of genus and specific difference is a single reality likewise, so there must be between them a need, so one of them is a cause of the other, and the genus is not a cause of the specific difference, otherwise it would necessitate it and the genus would be confined to a single species, or we would say: the specific differences were opposite necessary for a single thing, and both are false. So the specific difference is the cause of the genus, and that is the desired conclusion. And it was answered about it that the thing needed is the incomplete cause and that it does not necessitate its effect, then if you mean by cause the complete cause, we deny that one of them is a cause of the other, and the need that must be established between the parts does not necessitate it, i.e., that one of them is a complete cause of the other, and that is apparent. And if you mean by cause the incomplete cause, then perhaps the genus is an incomplete cause of the specific difference, and its necessitation of its effect is not necessary, only the complete cause necessitates the effect, so the confinement of the genus to a single species does not follow, nor that opposite specific differences are necessary for a single thing.
(The glosses: He said: (and there is no doubt etc.) he indicated by presupposing this premise that in the expression of the text there is ellipsis by contextual indication, and this is according to the view of those who say that the predicated parts are distinct in external reality, whether they are united in existence or not; but according to the view of those who say they are abstracted, there is nothing in external reality except the simple identity, and the composition from them is mental. He said: (a single reality likewise) i.e., with real unity, i.e., disregarding the consideration of the considerer; according to the view of those who say the essence is composed from predicated parts in external reality, its being described with unity is in external reality; according to the view of those who say it is abstracted and composition is only in the mind, its being described with it is in the mind. He said: (and the genus would be confined etc.) because it is a cause in terms of its correlation with the effect for the composition of the real essence from them, so its nature is not found separated from it; if one considers that a single nature does not necessitate two things. He said: (either from one side it can be included in the negation of circularity, but the more apparent is that his statement: such that it does not entail circularity is when the need is from both sides. He said: (and there is no doubt that the essence composed of genus and specific difference is a single reality likewise) it was said: if we make 'reality' as predicate, the proposition becomes indefinite because among composites there are conventional realities, which are unsuitable; so the way is to make it as a distinction or a state, and 'one' is the predicate so that the proposition is universal, not indefinite. He said: (so one of them is a cause of the other) the intended meaning of cause is that on which the thing depends in general, so it includes the condition, and the objection does not arise from it; indeed, his statement that the genus is not a cause of the specific difference etc. is repelled, as will be clarified. He said: (or we say) the intended meaning of the alternation is to make the listener choose between the two expressions in necessitating the corruption.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This is an extended passage containing the philosophers' proof that in a composite essence, one part must be the cause of the other, leading to the conclusion that the specific difference is the cause of the genus. The passage then presents an objection and its answer. The commentary glosses inserted explain various linguistic and philosophical points. The core argument: The essence composed of genus and specific difference is a single reality, so there must be need between them; one must be the cause. The genus cannot be the cause, otherwise it would necessitate the specific difference, leading to absurdities. Therefore, the specific difference is the cause. The objection: The needed thing is only the incomplete cause, which does not necessitate its effect. The answer: If 'cause' means complete cause, we deny that one part is a complete cause of the other; the need does not require completeness. If 'cause' means incomplete cause, then perhaps the genus is an incomplete cause of the specific difference, and this does not necessitate the problematic consequences; only the complete cause necessitates. Thus the confinement of genus and the necessary opposite differences do not follow.

Key Terms
جنس
فصل
علة
ماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that in a composite essence the genus is the cause of the specific difference because genus is broader.
Correction: The passage shows that if genus were cause, it would be limited to one species, contradicting its universality. Therefore, the specific difference must be the cause.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, which of the following is NOT an absurdity if the genus were the cause of the specific difference?
A) The genus would be confined to a single species.
B) Opposite specific differences would be necessary for one thing.
C) The specific difference would be independent of the genus.
D) Both A and B.

Key Takeaway
A composite essence's real unity implies a causal relation; the specific difference must be the cause because the genus cannot be without absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are a composite of many traits and beliefs. What is the one 'specific difference' that, if it were absent, would unravel the very core of who you are? Does your daily life demonstrate that you treat this as the cause of your other qualities?
?
The philosophers argue that a real unity requires a causal relationship between parts. Consider your own commitments: is there a belief or action that you treat as merely an 'effect' of something else, when in truth it should be the 'cause' shaping your identity? What would change if you reversed that relationship?
?
If your genus (humanity) were the cause of your specific difference (e.g., your unique character), it would mean your distinctiveness is just a necessary consequence of being human—something automatic, not a choice. Do you live as though your specific difference is a passive outcome or as an active cause that defines and limits your humanity? How would you need to change if you truly believed your specific difference is the cause of your genus?

Objection and Answer: Incomplete vs Complete Cause
Objection and answer distinguishing complete and incomplete cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the distinction between complete and incomplete cause resolves the objection against the proof that the specific difference is the cause of the genus.

Core Idea
The objection fails because it confuses complete cause (necessitates) with incomplete cause (does not necessitate).

The previous proof concluded that specific difference is the cause of genus. An objection arises: perhaps the cause meant is only an incomplete cause, which does not necessitate its effect. The answer clarifies the distinction between complete and incomplete cause, showing that the proof's reasoning only requires an incomplete cause, avoiding the absurdities.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector argues that the needed thing is only an incomplete cause, which does not necessitate its effect. So the earlier argument that genus cannot be cause because it would necessitate absurdities might not hold.
2
Distinguish complete vs incomplete cause
The answer first states that if 'cause' means complete cause, then we deny that one part is a complete cause of the other; the need between parts does not require completeness.
3
Apply the distinction to the genus possibility
If 'cause' means incomplete cause, then the genus might be an incomplete cause of the specific difference, and this does not necessitate the effect. Thus, the earlier absurdities (confinement of genus, opposite differences) do not follow, because those follow only from a complete cause.
4
Conclusion
Therefore, the proof that specific difference is the cause (in the relevant sense) remains valid, and the objection is neutralized.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that any causation between genus and specific difference must be complete and necessitating.
Correction: The passage shows that only complete cause necessitates; incomplete cause does not, so the genus could be an incomplete cause without the problematic consequences.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, if one means by 'cause' the incomplete cause, what follows regarding the genus being a cause of the specific difference?
A) The genus definitely is a complete cause.
B) The genus might be an incomplete cause, and this does not necessitate the effect.
C) The genus cannot be any kind of cause.
D) The genus becomes the specific difference.

Key Takeaway
Distinguishing complete cause (necessitates) from incomplete cause (does not necessitate) resolves the objection and preserves the proof that specific difference is the cause in the relevant sense.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own reasoning about causes—whether in daily life or in worship—do you often assume that a partial factor is the complete cause? Is there an area where you've mistakenly thought that because A is present, B must follow, ignoring that A might be only an incomplete cause?
?
Consider a time when you attributed a success or failure entirely to one thing (e.g., hard work, luck, or even Allah's decree). How might the distinction between complete and incomplete cause adjust your perspective and increase your reliance on Allah as the only complete cause?
?
When you face an argument that seems to refute a truth you hold, do you quickly accept it, or do you look for hidden distinctions (like complete vs. incomplete cause) that could resolve the objection? What would it take for you to develop the scholarly habit of examining possible distinctions before conceding?
